Date      : Sep 24, 2011 at 2:49 PM

OK,  the boxes are mounted to the frame.  the boxes are 1/2 inch sintra glued and screwed together.  the armature is One inch  thick wall pipe.  Very strong stuff.   drilled and bolted to the boxes.  heres what i have so far.

Thanks for looking.

Al

Post #44  (forum post #1940943)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Oct 10, 2011 at 6:36 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Hi,  Sintra is a foamed PVC sheet. Its what the studio used. It easy to work with and glues easy.  It easily countersinks the screws.  Its great stuff,  better and lighter than acrylic.

Al

Post #82  (forum post #1992972)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Nov 10, 2011 at 6:06 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Just tried a Different Primer,  Normally i use Duplicolor.  which its not bad, not as good as it used to be, but good enough.  The other day  i ran out so i decided to try the Rustoleum filler primer.  an wow it worked great,  dried fast and didnt clog the paper at all.  and its cheaper than the duplicolor.  and can get it at home depot.  just thought you guys might like to know, for you builders out there.

Al

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Got some molds done, came out great,  brushed the first coat on to get the silicone into all the fine details to ensure no air bubbles.  then vibrated the table for a few minutes to lift any air bubbles to the top.  Next will Gel coat the molds and lay up Epoxy fiberglass for the parts.

  Thanks for looking.

 Al

Post #182  (forum post #2105297)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Jan 22, 2012 at 1:46 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks Clay.

    Another update,    made a disposable concrete mold for a vac pattern.  took original pattern  waxed it,  one layer of tooling concrete let set up.  then remove pattern  re wax mold.  next pour more concrete reinforced with burlap  let set up and remove.  and you have a solid piece of tooling concrete you can use for a Vacuum pattern that will out last anything else.  only thing to remember is let the concrete fully dry before you use it.  Also total cost for the mold. under $2.00

  Also Jason finished Lathing the small part for the main Cargo box.

 Thanks for looking.

I broke it up into two parts so it will be a sharper part instead of forming it as one and lose the detail at the Base.

Post #202  (forum post #2123426)

Damn Al, how do you keep that round?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #203  (forum post #2123472)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Feb 5, 2012 at 6:38 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

RickDTM said:

			Damn Al, how do you keep that round?
		

Click to expand...

  Rick,

       What you do is first make a sturdy pattern.  map it out.  put in the center a brass tube, then add another brass tube to telescope into the tube in the pattern to make a sweep.  it takes a few coats of bondo to get it smooth.

      OK.  heres a trick to working with bondo.  ive read alot of threads where every one says i hate bondo its so hard to work with.   they all prefer Evercoat.    well  heres the trick to ever coat.  all it is is Bondo with a lot of resin in it.    you can make your own evercoat by adding Fiberglass resin to regular bondo to make it smooth.  the more you add the smoother it gets.

  I cant see spending that outrageous amount for such a small amount of Evercoat when i can make my own.   There are a few products you can buy to smooth out bondo  but its basically resin.

    Heres the pattern with the sweep,  i spread bondo over the whole thing and then put the sweep in and go around a few times until smooth. Carefully remove the sweep and let dry.  if you do it right shouldnt take much sanding to get a nice smooth finish.

  Thanks for Looking.

Al

[IMAGE: bettyconepattern32027.jpg]

Post #208  (forum post #2132875)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Feb 12, 2012 at 11:33 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

OK, finally got some Parts laid up in Epoxy.  it was very cold but managed to get them made with only a few minor air bubbles. And started on the base for the cone.  did a quick trim of the parts and a mock up.

   Parts are made from white Gel coat and smooth on epoximite Medium set Epoxy.   one recommendation i would make for any one doing gel coat work is to get a good Industrial gel coat.  dont use a cheap boat gel coat  it wont stick to the mold very well.   Just my two cents.

  Thanks for looking.

Al

Post #229  (forum post #2151026)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Feb 26, 2012 at 9:18 AM
Reactions : Like — Atlanthia
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Small update today,  camera battery died so this was all i was able to get.

  Started on the vac part that goes behind the cone.   got the edges nice and sharp.  still have to chop the other pull to sit on top of this one to give it the layered effect and scribe panel lines.  the little black marks on the plastic are pencil marks,  i run the pencil over the part then sand with some 320 to see any low spots.  its a quick and cheap way to guide coat it to find flaws.

   Will have the main cargo box molded and should have the parts mounted by next weekend.  should have enough silicone to also mould the rear part, but we will see.  more soon.  

Thanks for looking.

Al

Post #277  (forum post #2181279)
Author    : Shizman
Date      : Mar 19, 2012 at 9:33 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

This is awesome.

What gel coat do you personally use?  Is there a specific technique you use when adding your layers?  I.e. do you apply the gel coat, then wait a certain time frame, then lay in your glass, then apply the epoxy?  I want to try your technique.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #278  (forum post #2181314)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Mar 19, 2012 at 9:55 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks Jerry, such a comedian.

Shizman,  ill have to get back to you on the part numbers for the gel coat.  But what i do is. Mix the gel coat i like to use my fingers to push the gel coat into all the fine details to make sure i get all the air out (no bubbles) then use a chip brush to spread the rest out.  Heres the trick to no air bubles in the gel. Take a heat gun and lightly warm the gel coat up and brush it smooth. The heat brings all the bubbles to the surface and just brush them out.   Let dry until tacky/ firm about 20 to 30 mins depending on your temp.  The lightly wet out the gel coat with epoxy. And add your mat. And repeat depending on how many layers you want. I usually do 2 to 3.  Also. Dont over soak the mat. The drier the part the stronger it is.

Hope that helps,  if you need anything else feel free to PM me 

Al
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #279  (forum post #2181317)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Mar 19, 2012 at 9:58 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Oh yeah. When using a heat gun on the gelcoat. Do it very quickly. No more than 45 seconds. Dont want to accelerate the curing and have a bad part.  Keep it moving and dont concentrate the heat in one spot for to long.

Al
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #311  (forum post #2195811)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Mar 30, 2012 at 5:38 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ray22 said:

			How thick did you go on the plastic for the cone Al 2 or 3mm?
		

Click to expand...

  We used 3mm for the base.  and going to use a mix of thinner plastic to build up the layers on the cone to get the desired effect.  still have a few more pulls.  have to adjust the fomer because the cones so big,  i need to put bigger guide rails to get a smooth transition onto the pattern with the plastic.   right now one or two have a slight sag at the top.  no big deal, but it bothers so im going to fix it.

Al

Post #313  (forum post #2197362)
Author    : Stormy320
Date      : Mar 31, 2012 at 4:24 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

How did you sand the cargo box styrene edges so nice and uniform ?
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #314  (forum post #2197396)
Author    : Ray22
Date      : Mar 31, 2012 at 5:05 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Damn Al you are rolling like thunder on this your Bigtime brother!
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #315  (forum post #2197423)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Mar 31, 2012 at 5:29 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks guys.

    Stormy.  i use autobody sand paper.  continuous sheet roll its sticky on the back and i cut several pieces of left over sintra in different sizes depending on what im sanding and stick the paper to that.  i have a few with rougher grits and some with finer grits.  works great for a nice flat sanding block.  ill take a few pics of them next post.  if you look back at earlier posts you might see a few in the pics.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

   Shizman.  im sorry i forget to get you that gelcoat.  Smooth-on sells it buts its not by them.  its an industrial gelcoat.  i picked white because thats what the studio used for theres, plus it looks a lot cleaner and easier to see plus when you glue styrene on it it all blends in and has an even look to it.

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

faustus100 said:

			Truly amazing work!Learning so much from you!

Quick(and probably lame)question.

What method do you use to get really even and flush contours cuts?

[IMAGE: bettylittleboxes034.jpg]

Click to expand...

  Faustus,   all i used was a little drum sander attachment on a dremel and curled up a piece of sandpaper and slowly fit it into place.   i marked out about what i thought would need trimming and then slowly worked it down until it fit.  takes a few minutes but worth it so i didnt have to use filler.

Al
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #512  (forum post #2332636)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Jun 28, 2012 at 10:36 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

More on the betty tonight.

   but wanted to pass along this little trick for casting from an old mold.   we have a few molds at work that are old and probably should be re done but well no time right now.   they still release fine.  but even thought there keyed they just dont stay together like they should. and it leaks ( i should mention its a 3 part mold).   well theres a little trick i learned from a guy at the studio when i was out there.   never had a chance to use it until today.     put a little vaseline on the mold were the halves contact each other.  make sure not to get any where the resin will be.   it adds just enough stiction.  yeah thats a word.   to allow the resin to not leak out.   and 3 parts later and im good to go.

Al
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #578  (forum post #2416020)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Aug 13, 2012 at 5:43 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Talkierg said:

			Hi,I really enjoy every of your progress,nice work,especially molding n casting cause now Im on the progress learning that.

May I ask,I can see youre not using any pressure machine on your molding,n I see your molding like totally out of bubbles,how you do

that,can you give some tips on doing molding please,thanks.

:behave
		

Click to expand...

    What i do is mix the silicone.  do the long pour.  with a very thin stream, that will help break up any air.  pour into the lowest spot or tilt the mold and pour into the corner.  let the silicone find its own level.  by doing this it will fill slowly and force the air out.  once the mold is filled i like to tap it on the table for a few minutes to help any remaining air trapped work its way out.

 as for  a vacuum pump i just picked one up a week ago.  for the bigger molds i need a little more help.  so i degas the silicone.

Al
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #620  (forum post #2480337)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Sep 18, 2012 at 4:51 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks.

   Started molding the actuator and the main engine support arm.    Im molding the actuator in Silicone and the engine is an old school ultracal  mold.  theres no detail its a smooth part so theres no need to waste silicone on this..  just wax the ultracal and lay up the Epoxy glass.  the ultracal is great stuff if you take your time with it you can get really great molds that last a long time with no bubbles.  heres a bunch pics.

 Thanks for looking.

Al

Post #654  (forum post #2535372)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Oct 18, 2012 at 2:55 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Really glad i could help out and glad you guys like my stuff.  

Be on the look out in about a year or sooner for a studio scale how to book. 

It will have all the Techniques the pros use and a bunch of mini articles on alot of famous movie models written by the model maker who built it.

As for the fiberglass i use.  Its a medium duty cloth.  I like between 6 and 7.5 ounce  cloth for parts. You get a strong but light part.   And as i always say. If you ever need any help just PM me. Always willing to share what i know.

Al

Got more done on the Tail and the wings.   the basic shape is carved out on Foam,  a liitle bondo and a first coat of heavy build (Sandy) primer.  stuff works great for patterns.   first coat was a light one.  i ran out of reducer so couldnt lay on a good coat like i wanted too.

   Also,  did a little test of a 3-d printer i picked up.  looks like it will be good for low rez patterns.

Post #691  (forum post #2618858)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : Dec 3, 2012 at 6:02 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Cadeus said:

			That is very cool.  what kind of foam are you using?  it almost looks like balsa foam.  Please keep up the great work!  We love it! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Click to expand...

  Thanks Guys,

    Its Urethane foam,  about 10 pound density.  stuffs great  you can carve it, sand it.  apply almost anything to it.  prime and paint.  of even glass over it.  great for patterns.   

  after another coat of heavy primer i will shoot some grey primer and then mold it in silicone.

Al

Hey Master Chief,

I only discovered this thread this morning and it's been captivating. It would be a shame if this never got completed —so I apologize if I'm out of line here or for asking a dumb question— but have you considered a Kickstarter campaign? 

I was personally able to get materials funded for a metal shaping project at KS (copper is uber $$$ so I reached out for some crowd funding). Granted, what I raised probably doesn't nearly equate to what you may need, but it's definitely free to try. You could offer your book as one of the tier level gifts for supporters, small resin castings for lower tier support, etc.. Hell, if your original benefactor has backed out completely, you could offer the model herself to a top-tier funder (what that number is I have no clue, but I've seen crazy numbers get funding for much less valuable objects). 

Anyway, I don't know if there are any design patents or copyright issues involved, but the Kickstarter community is keen on seeing art projects getting finished. This certainly qualifies and you certainly deserve every possible opportunity to see this through. 

~Chaz

This is very cool I worked on this film as a model maker. I may have some photos that might help you. I will look through what I have.  I did not do much on the Betty  Though it sat right next to my desk when it was being built. I did work on a special close up model of the ship for the docking scene also woked on the dock..  I was on set with it for the first part of the miniature shoot as well.  We put the miniature cockpit in the model on set.  The orignal plan had been to do all those shots as green screen, but when it got to set they changed their mind and had us do a practical miniature that could be seen through the windows.I will see what iIcan find that might not be on line but now days everyting is on line.

Post #797  (forum post #3599245)
Author    : Hopson
Date      : Mar 27, 2015 at 4:42 PM
Reactions : Like — MonsieurTox
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

The landing  bay was a big model but it was tall and not hard to get around.  The 1/6 scale lab and Alien cells was huge, the size of room.  It took up a huge amout of space in the shop. You got so used to going through it or around it to get to tools and supplies. The day they moved it to set every time I crossed into the space it had been sittting it it felt like I was falling 

The model shoot for this film was crazy the DP had this idea that because space was black he needed to to use black bounce cards to light the models. It was insanely hot on set and we had huge lights on set to get enough light to see the models becuse of the balck bounce cards the models were literally smoking and melting. Bounce cards and drapes were catching on fire becuse it was so hot. Tempers were on a hair tirger, and fights between crew membrs and temper tantrams of all kinds were common. I was kind of glad that I was not on the shoot for the whole job.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

In the photo above with the two guys woking on the Betty not sure who the older guys is, but the younger man is Dale Tanguay he was a mechanical engineer on this film. One of the guys in the fabrication dept. named Randy nick named Dale "Kooky". Every time Dale came out into the main shop Randy would do this call Koooo Keeee!  The whole shop would take it up. Dale hated it. Which of course made it funnier. Shops can be like school yards. You either roll with it or you are doomed.

Post #807  (forum post #3601992)
Author    : Hopson
Date      : Mar 30, 2015 at 9:54 PM
Reactions : Like — LukaFilm, Randy13
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Here is another story from that job. I came to HGI to do a bit of a side job the opening title sequence for" Men In Black" I was working on model cars and trucks to run down a miniature desert scape. I did a nice replica of the illegal alien van for that and everyone loved that thing. They would come by and go this is so cool and I would think, You guys are working on space ships that is cool. These are just car models. So after that job ended I got hired for AR.  

One of my first projects was taking a vacuem formed shell of the closeup Betty and detailing it like the small ship.   Matt decided to directly supervise me on this job.  He would come out every hour or so and tell me well this is good but I needed to do less detail and speed it up. So I would do what he said.  Then when he came out the next time he would say the exact opisoite thing more detail slow down.  So I would do  that. It went back and fourth like this for the whole ten hour day. By the end of the day I was really sick of it. So sick of it I was ready to pick up my tools and walk away form there forever.  He came out and walked over to me.  I looked at him put my tools down and steped away  from the desk and said.  "Yes Matt?" he looked at me he looked at the model and said" Nice job". and walked away.   The next day he gave the job to another new model maker, and did the same thing to him all day. I'm not sure if it was his way of breaking in new model makers. It was not the last time he did that kind of thing to me.

I did lots of jobs for them.  It is part of the reason I stopped working at HGI. The last job I did for them this kind of thing happed. I remember Adam Gilbart walked over to me and said "Did he just yell at you for doing a good job?" I said "Yep." Adam walked away saying " That is one of the craziest things I have ever seen." For years after I had this piece of paper with Adam's quote was taped in the top of my tool box.  "Did he just yell at you for doing a good job?" It may still be there I do not use that box much anymore.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #824  (forum post #3634266)
Author    : IEDBOUNTYHUNTER
Date      : May 3, 2015 at 1:48 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

OK  im Back.    had a few bucks to spend so i bought some silicone and resin and cast a few parts. and started on the main engine.    I really love shaping patterns  its  fun and for me very relaxing.   so  heres  a bunch of pics of what i did today.    

  I molded and cast the 4 engine pistons

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2015.04.23_zpsybw53shg.jpg]

And heres the vac plug for the wings engine.   I made the pattern and did a tooling concrete mold.

[IMAGE: 2015-05-01%2010.31.04_zpsmihnttzq.jpg]

[IMAGE: 2015-05-01%2011.04.20_zpstrj2jtj0.jpg]

And the final part to use on the vac table.

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2015.03.52_zpsl2nsgb8q.jpg]

And for the biggen of them all.  the main engine is started    its made from Urethane foam and coated in bondo.   once i get it all trued up  i will cut in all the details and mold this baby.   Heres a few a pics.

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2011.24.13_zpsc2kqottr.jpg]

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2011.25.10_zpskzmhn30w.jpg]

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2012.30.00_zpsaibjwgmf.jpg]

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2013.25.24_zpsxtlaivpz.jpg]

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2013.25.46_zpswtwfuqwq.jpg]

[IMAGE: 2015-05-03%2013.25.56_zpslipxrcov.jpg]

   I nailed the shape perfectly on the engine.  I just need to sand in the fine details and  spray a nice heavy coat of Sandy primer on this and it will be ready to mold.  

  Thanks for checking this out.  any questions or comments please feel free to comment or send me a PM.
